#  [](/thread/308230-gann-pvs-price-vibration-system-trading)Gann PVS (Price vibration System) Trading 

  * 

  * [#1](/thread/308230-gann-pvs-price-vibration-system-trading "Post Permalink")

  * First Post: Edited Feb 16, 2012 3:11pm  Aug 6, 2011 6:47pm | Edited Feb 16, 2012 3:11pm 

  * [ moneydeep](moneydeep)

  * Joined Jun 2011 | Status: Trader | [139 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=183360)

I've been wandering around this forum for a while and been trading for around a year now. Still learning lots of stuff. I like to help others so posting this.  
  
I call this the Gann Price vibration system. It is not a system by itself but is more a confirmation system. Add this to whatever method you trade and it will help you for sure.  
It's based on the gann wheel. From a low you can predict possible points where the market will vibrate to. Same with a high. Price will either bounce off, gap through, or blow through these levels. Thats why I call it a confirmation system.  
I have attached an excel file in which you input a significant low and a high and it gives you price vibration levels. (remove the decimals when inputing the numbers) eg: 1.4320 would be 14320  
Then just add the lines to you mt4 chart and you have areas to watch.   
Sometimes you may just have a low you can still plot higher levels and predict vibration areas.  
It works on any timeframe. I personally like to take the daily and draw my lines so I can use them interday for a long time without having to change them.

  1. It's also interesting to know that many times price reverses at these levels to the tick.
  2. Also note that when there are 2 lines in close proximity the area is stronger.

  
Update 1  
Added a video showing how to do it. Sorry for the low quality. Hope you get the idea.  
  

Inserted Video

  
  
Update 2   
  
Updated indicator can be found here thanks to brooky29  
  
[http://www.forexfactory.com/showthre...33#post5389333](http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=5389333#post5389333)

  * [#26](/thread/post/5338391#post5338391 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 30, 2012 11:07pm  Jan 30, 2012 11:07pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar124529_2.gif) brooky29](brooky29)

  * | Commercial User  | Joined Nov 2009 | [51 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=124529)

Hi all.  
I was intrigued by the calculations that MoneyDeep was using so I knocked up an indicator that would automatically show the first circle lines which seem to be the most used. I have checked it against MoneyDeeps calcs and it appears to be correct. If not the code is exposed and changeable. It is all longhand code because I wrote it as I saw it so if someone wants to loop it, be my guest.  
  
Charts below explain how it works, but essentially, when you load the indicator you will see a red vertical control bar under the last candle and some horizontal lines.  
  
Just select the start or end of that red line and place it on whatever High or Low you want. The horizontal lines will adjust per MoneyDeeps calculations. ( Assuming I read the spreadsheet correctly :-)  
  
You can open a bigger timeframe and use Highs and Lows from it if you want and then back down to a smaller tf without the lines moving. I need to not lose the Red line when you change tf's and the payback for that is that you have to delete this line when unloading the indicator. All other lines etc will unload.  
  
Hope this helps.  
Cheers  
Brooky

  * [#29](/thread/post/5387608#post5387608 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 16, 2012 12:50am  Feb 16, 2012 12:50am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar124529_2.gif) brooky29](brooky29)

  * | Commercial User  | Joined Nov 2009 | [51 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=124529)

Hi All.  
  
I was asked to make the indicator into an Auto version so that one could quickly apply it to many charts consistently at say the high and low of 2 or 3 days ago.  
  
Attached is the indicator with this option able to be set. You can still use it manually if you turn UseAutoTfHiLos off, but it is on by default.  
  
Inputs are as below.  
extern bool UseAutoTfHiLos = true;  
extern int AutoTf2Use = 1440;  
extern int MtfBarBack = 1;  
  
AutoTf2Use obviously needs to bigger than the tf the chart is on and the MtfBarBack option tells the indi which MTF Bar (Day or H4 etc) it should take the levels from.  
  
Cheers  
Brooky

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar124529_2.gif) brooky29](brooky29)

  * | Commercial User  | Joined Nov 2009 | [51 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=124529)

Hi again.  
  
While I don't trade this concept, I am a big believer in Fib confluence and all that.  
  
It occurred to me that if you have several copies of the indi on chart with either different MTF bars back or different periods that you would have the benefit of confluence on one chart.  
  
The updated indicator allows you to do this by simply putting a different letter in the option  
extern string IndiCopyOnChart = "a";   
  
Example chart uses 4 copies of the indi called a.b.c and d. They are set at H4, Daily, Weekly and Monthly and all displayed on an M15 chart.  
  
For those that understand these levels, I imagine that this is beneficial.  
Cheers  
Brooky.

Hello.  
  
I have had a chance to tidy up the code and work on the color options. This version should be the last unless some bugs crawl out.  
You can now properly change colors and styles for different timeframes.  
Tpl attached of a Multi Timeframe setup with H4, Daily, Weekly and Monthly all on the same chart.  
Mousing over a line will let you know what Timeframe it belongs to.  
Lines will readjust as each Timeframe plots a new bar.  
eg: H4 will readjust once every 4 hours etc.  
  
Confluence is instantly visible. It would be nice to see someone come up with the trade strategy now. Thanks to MoneyDeep for the idea. @ MoneyDeep. You may want to put this version on your front post to stop the inevitable newbie, what version should I use questions.  
Cheers  
Brooky

Well Moneydeep; as you know, we have half of the puzzle done here. We have charted price levels, now the most interesting addition is TIME confluence. When time & price are in confluence, expect a big bang.  
So, off each high and low, count 45 bars, 90 bars, 180 bars and 360 bars into the future to plot the time cycles. Then watch the fireworks when the major time markers line up with the major price levels...it's uncanny how deadly accurate they can be.  
Can an time indicator be created to acomplish this?

Hi  
Excellent suggestion. I can have a look at picking possibly HH and LL each day of the past x days and automate a series of fib timelines that would do this.  
  
For the moment because it is probably more accurate visually, you could use the Fib Timelines tool in MT4 set to 0,1,2,4,8 and pull the 0 to 1 line over 45 bars and as you say, watch the magic.  
  
I have 2 sets on highs in yellow to indicate they are on highs and 2 on green which are on lows.  
  
Pic attached with a circle of where the timeline was started and an arrow to where it was pulled to (45 bars). Indeed the magic appears. Point to note is that both the point 2 longs( current) and shorts (previous) where projected 4 days ago. I think they call that a leading indicator :-)  
  
I will have a look at the day high low idea when I get a moment.  
Cheers  
Brooky.

I think you are on the right track...however there may be too many lines on the chart to pick from. So I think that the swing highs/lows that your original indicator gets is probably correct... That is how the original Gann Wheel is calculated...Take the recent high and plot 45^ from there to get the price. Then when you count the bars forward from that recent high you arrive at the future bar then plot that.   
Then you would do the same exercise for the recent swing low.

So we have to establish a timeframe to use consistently.

  * Feb 23, 2012 5:02am  Feb 23, 2012 5:02am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar124529_2.gif) brooky29](brooky29)

  * | Commercial User  | Joined Nov 2009 | [51 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=124529)

Hi all.  
Updated indicator includes.  
  
1) All the stuff it had before :-)  
  
2) Option to show Bar cycles of your length from auto MTF start point or where you manually place the control bar.  
  
3) Option to turn on a double Gann Grid that will auto calculate from the Cycle period that you enter.  
  
4) All objects should ( if I got it right ) be available to each copy you put on chart as long as you change the alpha character for each copy on chart as before.  
  
Now that there are a larger amount of variables, it would be very helpful if those that really get Gann to assist in the correction of any default values. If they could mention them here, I can hardcode a viable starting set into the indicator.  
  
If something goes wrong with the code, just pop a note up on the thread and I will attend to it.  
  
Cheers  
Brooky.

If traders cannot manually work the excel file given in the beginning of this thread, most likely you guys wont find consistency using this method. The first indicator Brooky made is perfect enough and yet traders wants it curve fitted because they don't understand how to use it. Gann did not give hard rules for traders to follow because that would be too easy but instead he left clues in all of his writings for us to decipher. This is why I'm so hesitant to put up charts because I don't think anyone on this thread read any of Gann's books at all. Applying GannSq9 without knowing its context and true formula is the biggest fallacy of all. I would suggest traders strap them self down because Gann's techniques takes years to master.   
  
Good Luck To Everybody's Grueling Journey.

Allonso and others Hi,  
I still monitor the thread and get pm's from guys who want to know things, so if I get a message that something needs clearing up I am happy to help.  
As you may have read earlier in the thread, I do not use this indicator in my own trading, however I do use some of the logic entwined with other indicators.   
I was actually hoping for some more Gann related charts from active Gann traders, but it seems as if Gann officienados are very secretive about such things, Much more than regular traders with regular systems.  
With regard to the cycle lines jumping, I can only assume that you are moving the bar and then watching the cycles jump back to where they were on the next tick. If that is the case then the option UseAutoTfHiLos needs to be turned OFF. That should keep the cycles in position.  
In the interests of adding to the discussion, I will prepare a chart with my chosen supply demand style of trading and post it up as a way of adding another flavour into the mix.  
Cheers  
Brooky

  * [#70](/thread/post/5467558#post5467558 "Post Permalink")

  * Mar 13, 2012 3:16am  Mar 13, 2012 3:16am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar124529_2.gif) brooky29](brooky29)

  * | Commercial User  | Joined Nov 2009 | [51 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=124529)

Hi all.  
As mentioned before, I did up a chart with my way of picking a valid point to use for setting a grid up.  
Since I use supply and demand logic in my own trading, it seemed natural to use a very significant recent point of supply as a starter point for the bar, and for later levels, one would just follow the lower lows down by dragging the bottom of the control bar down.  
What I found interesting was the pinpoint timing of the lowest low of the NFP effect on a time cycle that was in place from the moment the first touch was made on the big supply bar up top many hours before.  
The chart has my notes on it, but it may be interesting when picking points in the past, to think of them as how important a rejection they were in terms of supply and demand.  
One can also see why today has been a ping pong match between the close supply and demand levels before supply was finally exhausted.  
I am still long from this morning so I am hoping they are in search of some more supply up north.  
I would love to hear from a Gann trader as to what their call would be in a situation like this.  
Cheers  
Brooky

Allonso  
  
Regarding changing the timing to M15:   
1) If the _UseAutoTfHiLos_ option is set to **true** , the indi will find the High and Low of that timeframe to set itself to. If you are using M15, I would suggest to leave it at any period bigger than that.  
  
2) If the _UseAutoTfHiLos_ option is set to **false** , you can achieve what I have on the chart because you can pull the control bar onto any bar of your choice and then elongate it to a relevant point as I have done.  
  
Re: "supply and demand logic bars". I do have a supply demand indi which has not been released as yet ( it will be commercial ), but this is just a general term used. If you want to know more about Supply and Demand, there are some good threads here or you can go to my website educational area where you can sign up for a whole stack of stuff that will explain it and much more in detail from the partnership we have with the online trading academy.  
  
Re: Line indi. If you do not want to share here you can always pm me and I can have a look for you.  
  
Cheers  
Brooky

Hi Brooky29,  
Thanks for the information on "Supply & Demand" will have a look at the appropriate threads and maybe your own website as well.  
  
I am quite OK with sharing the line mq4 but would advise anyone interested to not copy or use it in it's present state as they will not be very happy with some of the problems.  
  
As it is not related to Gann I suppose if I am allowed it would be sensible to start a thread to explain the theory and how I use it.  
  
Anyway the idea was to make an indicator that would place as many horizontal lines as required, from a selected starting point at a pre-selected spacing.  
It does everything I wanted except for the following:  
  
**1\. Delete all lines from the window, from the selection of any line. I thought that ObjectsDeleteAll(); would achieve it, but it doesent.**  
  
**2\. I have not found a way to replace the pre-selected spacing from a value of the type 0.005 to a simpler type 50 pips.**  
  
Other than that it does mainly what I intended, I can plot lines Up from a value or Down by adding a - sign in front of the selected spacing values.  
  
Hope it will not be too much trouble to ammend the code, it will also help me in my understaning of mq4 coding. As this was my first attempt I am quite pleased it at least does some of what I intended.  
  
Regards Allonso

I'm sorry I haven't been much active in the thread. I'ts because I was busy with personal matters. Also I am a novice/intermediate trader at best and was hoping that by starting this thread others would post their experiences using gann lines.   
  
Brooky has done a great job with the indicator and I use it for my daily analysis. (I don't use the latest one though).   
  
I am going through a time where I realised that I needed some inner peace and quiet to develop a system of trading that I feel comfortable with. This has kept me busy. I've been doing research on timing and hope to share it here someday.

Hi Moneydeep,  
  
Glad you dropped in and yes it would be great if you can post charts sometimes, it all helps the rest of us who are trying to find out how the Brooky29 indicator is helping with trading.  
I have read lots about Gann and his timing methods and the more I read the more confusing it becomes, there are so many times given, Calendar days, Trading Days, Weekly timing and so on. Even then I am not sure   
how it would apply to FX.  
However I have attached a chart of Brooky29's indicator with a Ganns 11 trading days setting. As can be seen the are quite a number of minor peaks that are either on a line or within two bars of it.  
Problem is that the lower the TD setting then inevitably we are going to get more hits and close approximations, and do we really want to know minor turns or are we after Intermediate and Major turning points.  
I am hoping that Brooky29's new indicator when ready may help to resolve some of these puzzles.  
  
Regards Allonso

Here is a pretty useful script that I use to delete objects from a chart with a single click.  
  
Put it in your experts/scripts folder, then just double click on it and all objects will be removed from your chart.

  * Mar 17, 2012 9:44pm  Mar 17, 2012 9:44pm 

  * [ Belmont](belmont)

  * | Joined Mar 2012  | Status: Trader | [44 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=238123)

Thank you for the topic, it made me register to the forum. As you've pointed out already, the problem with Gann is the time factor. Gann experts are super-secretive about timing. The rest is pretty basic maths, we can draw lots of s/r lines in hindsight, but will be lost at trading them in real time.  
  
There is a distinction in the scale, which is not clear enough in the original Excel sheet and it's even more blurred in the indicator's settings. We can divide a circle in halves (then quarters, eighths etc.) _or_ thirds (then sixths, twelfths etc.):  
  
i.e. 1/2, 1/4, 1/8 (50%, 25%, 12,5% or 180°, 90°, 25°);  
  
and 2/3, 1/3 (66,6%, 33,3% or 240°, 120°) etc.  
  
This normally yields more consistent results on an instrument. However, alternating the "major" levels (50% or 25% with 66,6% or 33,3%) might yield consistent results as well. All depends on the definitions, though. For instance, 50% might mean half (or twice) the current price – or halfway between a chosen price swing. I have yet to test the sheet and the indicator based on an instrument's all time high or all time low, looking for confluence.  
  
Apart from these, I couldn't find anything else consistent enough when it comes to Gann expertise. And as I mentioned, this is all pretty useless without knowing how to calculate the time factor.

In a nutshell, when the current price candle on 1 hr chart closes above the gann line, i go long. Opposite for short, if candle on 1 hr closes below the gann line, maybe a good time to short.   
  
I also apply lots of filtering that has nothing to do with gann. Please see my thread here on how I trade: <http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?t=345808>

  * [#105](/thread/post/5490004#post5490004 "Post Permalink")

  * Mar 20, 2012 12:03am  Mar 20, 2012 12:03am 

  * [ allonso](allonso)

  * | Joined Mar 2012  | Status: Trader | [46 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=232733)

Hi All,  
  
I thought I would just submit this graphic of the Dow 1900-1998 as evidence that a mathmatical relationship does exist in the market and that Ganns sq9 method of projecting turning points does work.  
  
All Gann lines have been calculated from lows in 1903 for the high of 1929, and 1932 for the highs in 1973, 1987, 1997 and 1998. Solid blues are the low dates, dashed blue are the high dates and red is the lows levels  
  
Although not show as part of this graphic, I have also used the 1932 low to calculate the highs of 2000 and 2007, both levels were < 0.3% of the move up from the low that took 68 and 75 years.   
  
When you consider that over the total period of nearly 100 years, the constituents of the Dow must have changed on numerous occasions. How can it be argued that there is no mathmatical order in the markets and that Gann is just another fad.  
  
All those that unsure or downright sceptical should do the maths for themselves, prove to me that this is bunkum and I will give up trading and just play marbles.  
Allonso

  * Mar 22, 2012 6:14pm  Mar 22, 2012 6:14pm 

  * [ Belmont](belmont)

  * | Joined Mar 2012  | Status: Trader | [44 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=238123)

> [Quoting allonso](/thread/post/5497187#post5497187 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi All,  
>    
>  Does anyone know of an indicator that counts the number of bars between two points.  
>    
>  Allonso
> 
> Ignored

It's already in MT4. Use the crosshair tool (Ctrl+F), then click on one point on the chart and draw a line, it will display x/y/z, where  
x = number of bars between the two points,  
y = number of pips between the two points,  
z = the price under the pointer.  
  
Back to the thread, I again want to press the importance of the time factor (see [#90](http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=5485961#post5485961)). In most charting programs, including MT4, the so-called "Gann tools" are complete BS. They are graphical tools like the trendline tool, while Gann lines and angles are based on pure mathematical calculations. Change the timeframe on a chart and you'll see the "Gann" lines skip. Not to mention the data, different brokers open at different times and give you different data-feed, which can completely mess up your calculations. Any consistency you see just by drawing with your "Gann tools" is wishful thinking. Sorry if that sounds rude. Let's just base our ideas on the original Excel sheet. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

Hi All.  
The indicator attached can be simply used to calculate bars spanned, or in context of this thread, it will calculate the Degrees of the bars spanned and the pips covered by the range if you want.  
  
If you load it onto a chart, you can just park it out of the way in a corner until you need it again.  
  
When you load it, just double click on the rectangle and use the grab handles to push n pull it around.  
  
Some may want to position it in a Gannish spot as calculated by the angles and then manually draw some lines, fans cycles etc over/relevant to it, so it could be a handy addition to the ol tool chest for a variety of reasons.  
  
Colors placements sizes etc are all optioned.  
  
Cheers  
Brooky

  * [#137](/thread/post/5546946#post5546946 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 6, 2012 4:06am  Apr 6, 2012 4:06am 

  * [ allonso](allonso)

  * | Joined Mar 2012  | Status: Trader | [46 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=232733)

Hi Sparks60,  
  
I would be delighted to still take part in this thread, but when no one else can be bothered to join in and discuss Gann trading and ask questions which we can all brainstorm or even post their demo trades and research. It does then become very weird with the takers of this world hoping that someone else can provide them with the answer without them lifting a finger to contribute.  
  
I have notice many times that when I have logged on to the thread there is maybe one or two members viewing and three or four more who have not logged in or not yet joined ForexFactory. If some of these invisible viewers would come and join in we may eventually get somewhere.  
  
Now I have mentioned before that it seemed to me that if S/R levels can be mathematically calculated then there should also be a relationship with TIME.  
I read the other day on the web of a expectancy that the AUD/USD, which made a high on the 27/07/2011 should make another high on the 26/01/2012, these are calendar dates . As you can see from the Graphic it did'nt but it did make a high 67 days later on the 27/10/2011. Their date was in fact 65 days following the previous high, Whereas the high following their expected date on the 29/02/2012 was 90 days from the previous high.  
There are other relationships that fall on or near Gann numbers, in fact the largest error I have found is <1.5%. Starting with the Gann number 11 check multiples of this number up to 800. I checked From Feb 2001 to Feb 2003 -752 Daily Bars, error 0.366%. I suggest that you check them for yourself.  
  
I have also attached a sreenshot of the EUR/USD - 15min Tf which I like to trade and found that these relationships work there as well. I dont claim that they are accurate to the bar, but provide a framework to work within.  
  
Test it and discuss your findings.  
  
Allonso

  * [#143](/thread/post/5570726#post5570726 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 14, 2012 3:39am  Apr 14, 2012 3:39am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar69410_4.gif) Ilovepippin](ilovepippin)

  * Joined May 2008 | Status: Gannalist | [1,176 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=69410)

Thank you Zingers.  
  
Problem with Gann is that he did sooo much that how are you going to trade all that?  
  
Well, I can boil it down to one thing: Gann was a trend follower. Shocking right? ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)  
  
He had 1000 techniques to determine a change in trend, but the important thing is that **he traded the trend!** Which is what we want to do, trading. We are not in the business of forecasting.  
  
So how did he do that?  
Well, he used tools such as the square of 9 and his Gann lines.  
It is not so important to know how he got them, all we need to know is if it works or not. I'll shoot is straight up here, Gann used astro, but all this astro stuff boils down to mathematics which is easily drawn on a chart.  
Just like fibonacci numbers really. He said that: " In the end there are only mathematical points of force"  
  
Basically the trend is determined by the Gann lines, if price is following the line it is following the trend. On a break the trend changes.   
The Gann grid has very specific settings, but is not necessary for trading.   
What you want to do is determine the trend, if trend is up, buy the dips, if trend is down, sell the highs. Simple right? For that we need the lines and the square of 9. The SQ9 is a function of price, so that is easy. No hocus pocus required.  
  
To determine a change in trend we can use a simple oscillator. To calculate a future price point we can use the pythagoras theoreum.   
  
Then we need a dashboard to tell us how strong the trend is.   
Most important we need a solid money management system.   
  
I have a system in place that I trade manually. We can improve on that. I have a few indicators that we can combine into one to make it easy.   
  
That is really all it is. Gann was a very good swing trader and his method was simple.  
  
Cheers!

Trust me, there is no mortal soul on this planet that knows all the secrets of Gann.   
When Gann passed away he left truckloads of writings behind. Most of it purchased by the people from wdgann.com.  
But lots of his writings were lost.   
On top of that we can only know what he wrote down for us to decipher, which may not be everything he knew.   
  
However, it is not necessary to know everything to be a trader.   
Gann left us some plain and simple instructions and rules for successfull trading, not shrouded in any mysteries at all.  
  
Now, part 2 of your question. It is up to the trader to be successful. You need to be able to follow rules. No system is without losses. Gann lost trades as well. Traders are not all alike. One can have a system that works 100% for one person, and totally not work for another person.

> Ignored

Okay, the "Law of Vibration" what is that? Do we need to know what it is?  
We really don't, all we need to know is how we can apply it to trading.   
  
Ganns fundamental setup were his Gann lines. The basis of all his trading were these Gann lines which he used for trend determination.   
Now, there are 8 of them as there are 8 octaves in music. Thats a bit of the veiled language for you.   
The ones that are important are the 2x1, 1x1 and 1x2 for Forex.  
  
He drew these charts based upon a cycle. The cycle he used was 1 day for 1 cent.   
So, on a 4 digit platform that is 24h for 100 pips (for 5 digits multiply by 10). This is the 1x1 line.   
The 2x1 line is 100 pips for 12 hours and 1x2 is 100 pips for 36 hours.   
Draw these from a low ang high point.  
Above these lines, trend is up, below these line trend is down. Simple as that.  
  
It looks like this:

Size: 104 KB](/attachment/image/942342/thumbnail?d=1365758290)](/attachment/image/942342?d=1334420849)

The simple indi is the MACD or any oscillator that can detect divergence.   
If we can signal a divergence coming in the indi together with the Gann lines, we are well on our way.   
This is a good indicator of a direction change.  
Gann said to confirm the change of trend, this is one way.  
  
Next I'll post about cycles.

  * [#157](/thread/post/5573052#post5573052 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 8:23pm  Apr 15, 2012 5:25pm | Edited 8:23pm 

  * [ lotos7](lotos7)

  * | Joined Nov 2008  | Status: Trader | [90 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=86823)

Gann angles - a powerful tool for generating profits ...  
The method by which the analysis is based forex trading by using Gann angles, is one of the most popular, but at the same time challenging. But, despite this, the theory is often used to assess and predict the currency market. All indicators and methodological developments in the forex has its own characteristics. Forex Analysis according to the theory is no exception. Very often one can observe that the Gann angles mistaken for a trend line. And they are really very similar. Market fluctuations are clothed in a certain range. The top of the angles is the starting point of the incident trends, fluctuations in the base - the starting point of a growing trend.  
But in fact this is not the case and there are some differences. Gann Line represents a dynamic line that has the ability to move both on the horizontal axis and the vertical. This is not so obvious difference, but it's still there. Can be analyzed with the help of Forex charts, with the result that we can identify certain angle fluctuations of the stock, according to which we can define the limits of the speakers. But it is necessary to take into account that, if used to analyze too many corners, it can be confusing.  
On the whole theory of the Gann based on the following postulates, which are taken as a basis:  
A. Price, time and range of fluctuations in foreign exchange market  
Two. There is a certain geometric construction market, which is analyzed, it is possible to come to the conclusion that its subsequent motion  
Three. Markets are characterized by cyclical  
Gann believed that the market is a reflection of human nature, which is constant, so over time by analyzing past events, we can build based on their vision of the future.  
Using Gann angles, in practice,  
According to Gann's theories, the analysis of forex should be built on three models to help predict the behavior of the market in the future:  
A. The study. It is taken as the basis of historically recurring dates  
Two. Price range. It uses support and resistance lines, as well as the pivot point.  
Three. The plan of analysis.  
The application of this theory into practice requires a great deal of experience and knowledge, so here we noted the most important points to remember if you are using in their practice, such analysis forex.  
Decide which model you use in your trading. The most common models are the models 1, 2, and 1x2. Between these angles there is a definite difference in the slope of the lines. Overall, Gunn singled out a lot more angles. They are:  
\- 1 x 1 - 45 degrees  
\- 1 x 2 - 63.75 degrees  
\- 1 x 3 - 71.25 degrees  
\- 1 x 4 - 75 degrees  
\- 1 x 8 - 82.5 degrees  
\- 2 x 1 - 26.25 degrees  
\- 4 x 1 - 15 degrees  
\- 8 x 1 - 1.5 degrees  
In this case, the first variable is a unit of time, the second - a unit price. That is, according to the formula determined by the ratio between price and time interval.  
The value of the line 45 degrees  
According to Gann, this line is a line of long-term trend, it does not matter - ascending or descending. It is believed that if the price is above the ascending line, then the market is bullish mood. If the price is below the descending line, it is considered that the market holds a bearish mood. The intersection of the price of any of the lines will be talking about what is planned to change the trend. It should be noted that this line is a balance between price range and time. Quite often one can observe that when the price approaches the line, then the market is the balance of time and money. In addition, the chart can cause the channel, which should be placed parallel to the main trend line at a considerable distance from the extremes of the market.  
Under this line of the next line, which is based on the ratio of 2x1 shows that the two units of time has changed the price of one unit. In this case, line 4x1 will be even more shallow than line 2x 1.  
Gann Theory has some similarities with the fan-like lines, which are based on Fibonacci ratios. As the market moves up or down to adjust the angles to the existing tendency to form support and resistance levels.  
One notable method that is based on the theory of Gann - cardinal square, or "fundamental square method." This method is based on the concept of market analysis by reference to a certain size from as low as the price of the stock. This index can be calculated by conducting analysis of forex extended period of time, from several years to several decades. On the basis of such an operation is possible with a high probability to predict the location of support and resistance lines, which may appear in the future. The initial price is placed at the center of the square, then the correction as it is amended in a clockwise direction. Gradually, the horizontal and vertical lines form a cross in the center of the square. And the data that form the intersection is used as the likely support and resistance levels.

  * Apr 16, 2012 1:36am  Apr 16, 2012 1:36am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar69410_4.gif) Ilovepippin](ilovepippin)

  * Joined May 2008 | Status: Gannalist | [1,176 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=69410)

First we need to go back to middle school to understand how we measure time.  
We measure time as follows:  
The earth rotates one cycle around its axle and we call that a day.  
The earth orbits around the sun in 365.25 days and we call that a year.  
The moon orbits around the earth in 29.5 days and we call that a month. 12 months in a year, 365 days in a year.  
  
One orbit is 360 degrees. the earth travels 360/365= 0.98 degrees a day. For ease of use we will say 1 degree a day.   
  
Now the cycles:  
360 degree a day for one rotation = 360 degree per 24 hours that equals 4 minutes for one degree.   
This is the smallest cycle and very useful for intraday trading.   
  
If you work it out further to a workable cycle on a 15m intraday chart the 5 hour cycle works very well.   
5*60=300 minutes = 75 degrees of rotation 75*4.8=360.  
  
On the GBPUSD it nailed the top exactly and with Gann lines and MACD it looks like this.  
Nothing mysterious here. Just how everyone on earth is keeping time.

  * [ Uland.dx](uland.dx)

If you put the Gann Lines above or below the current action and look for places that they intersect you get areas of _possible_ change. On this chart I put the following angles.   
  
1x2  
2x3  
1x1  
3x2  
2x1  
  
you can see that direction changed nicely around each of the first 3 intersections.   
  
With that being said one of the problems with this type of analysis is that you can end up with so many lines on your charts you don't know what to do.

> [Quoting One day!](/thread/post/5575255#post5575255 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi OW,  
>    
>  Most of the above sounds doable, in fact this [indicator](http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=4933166#post4933166) already does some of what you want. The cycle values just need to be added into arrays and then a comparison function checks the count on each new bar - see the text in the bottom left of the chart.   
>    
>  Have you logged into Skype lately....  
>    
>  Regards
> 
> Ignored

  
My suggestion is to do this based upon the Gann timefactor which is earth rotation.   
You can add it to the existing arrays, but you have to be carefull not to get cluttered with lines.  
  
As I said, the 4 minute cycle is the smallest cycle. Use cycles with 4 minute intervals and use earth rotation degrees.  
  
45 degrees earth rotation is 3 hours = 180 minutes.  
90 degrees earth rotation is 6 hours = 360 minutes.  
120 degrees -- "" --- is 8 hours = 480 minutes.  
etc.  
1 day = 24 hours = 1440 minutes. (144 important number)  
  
Then add days to it as well.   
45 days, 90 days, 144 days etc.

I see your indi can measure price angle.  
That is interesting because price angles is what it is all about.   
  
If you can find the angle of current price action and can find a similar angle in the past, you can make a good prediction of where price is going.

  * [#183](/thread/post/5577565#post5577565 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 17, 2012 2:19am  Apr 17, 2012 2:19am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar69410_4.gif) Ilovepippin](ilovepippin)

  * Joined May 2008 | Status: Gannalist | [1,176 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=69410)

This morning it worked like a charm again.  
Divergence in the MACD, price stays above 1x1 Gannline.  
  
This time I added the Gann sq9 levels.  
These are a function of price.   
  
For 90 degrees price take the sqrt of the low = SQRT 1.2988= 113.965  
Add 0.5 = 113.965 + 0.5 = 114.465   
And multiply that by itself = 114.465 * 114.465 = 13102 = 1.3102  
  
For 45 degrees add 0.25  
For 180 degrees add 1  
For 360 degrees add 2 etc.

> [Quoting allonso](/thread/post/5580276#post5580276 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi One day,  
>    
>  Followed your video and it is now working, I did'nt realise that it only worked on the daily TF, I was trying to load it on the 15min TF which is what I like to trade.  
>  Can it be adapted to work on any TF as even the installed number set looks good on the Daily TF.

>    
>  Allonso
> 
> Ignored

It is designed to work on any timeframe, but if you start on the daily and then drop down to the 15min, you may not see anything unless you scroll to the left. If you want to use it on the 15min, I would have a second chart open and load the script and indicator onto that chart. That should work fine - you just need to remember that the array is only set up to plot a certain number of vertical lines. After that number has been reached you will just have a message in the bottom right corner informing you that the count has been completed.  
  
Hope that helps....

  * Apr 19, 2012 12:55am  Apr 19, 2012 12:55am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar69410_4.gif) Ilovepippin](ilovepippin)

  * Joined May 2008 | Status: Gannalist | [1,176 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=69410)

OK, time to add the next tool to the mix.  
Gann used a SQ9 technique to determine S/R.   
He squared the price fixed it to an aspect e.g., 90, 180, 270, 360 degrees and used those levels to determine buy/sell signals.  
  
Well, along comes this crazy mathemathician named Murrey and he basically figured out the same thing a different way.   
His levels are very usable for trading and coincide with the Gann levels almost exactly.  
  
So, as I said, sound has 8 octaves. Light has 7 different colors when you break it down. Gann has 8 lines, Murrey has 8 levels.   
It is very simple, When price gets closer to 7 or 8, a turn down can be expected. When price is closer to 1 or 2 a turn up can be expected.  
  
At either extreme a 50% retrace can be expected. 50% was Gann's favorite number. In Murrey Math it means the [4/8] level or 4th harmonic.  
  
Attached is the indi. Please experiment and backtest. 

Attached File(s)

![File Type: mq4](https://assets.faireconomy.media/images/attach/mq4.gif) [Murrey_Math_Line_X.mq4](/attachment/file/945076?d=1334764450) 13 KB | 1,134 downloads

I have been using Murrey's lines for some time.. I'll post later on what each line means..  
  
It's really good that we have ILP and all the others here to contribute and let us all learn bit by bit ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

  * [#212](/thread/post/5586915#post5586915 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 19, 2012 2:49am  Apr 19, 2012 2:49am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar241503_2.gif) kiranitoot](kiranitoot)

  * | Joined Mar 2012  | Status: Tip of the iceberg | [252 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=241503)

8/8 th's and 0/8 th's Lines (Ultimate Resistance)  
These lines are the hardest to penetrate on the way up, and give the greatest support on the way down. (Prices may never make it thru these lines).  
  
  
7/8 th's Line (Weak, Stall and Reverse)  
This line is weak. If prices run up too far too fast, and if they stall at this line they will reverse down fast. If prices do not stall at this line they will move up to the 8/8 th's line.  
  
  
6/8 th's and 2/8 th's Lines (Pivot, Reverse)  
These two lines are second only to the 4/8 th's line in their ability to force prices to reverse. This is true whether prices are moving up or down.  
  
  
5/8 th's Line (Top of Trading Range)  
The prices of all entities will spend 40% of the time moving between the 5/8 th's and 3/8 th's lines. If prices move above the 5/8 th's line and stay above it for 10 to 12 days, the entity is said to be selling at a premium to what one wants to pay for it and prices will tend to stay above this line in the "premium area". If, however, prices fall below the 5/8 th's line then they will tend to fall further looking for support at a lower level.  
  
  
4/8 th's Line (Major Support/Resistance)  
This line provides the greatest amount of support and resistance. This line has the greatest support when prices are above it and the greatest resistance when prices are below it. This price level is the best level to sell and buy against.  
  
  
3/8 th's Line (Bottom of Trading Range)  
If prices are below this line and moving upwards, this line is difficult to penetrate. If prices penetrate above this line and stay above this line for 10 to 12 days then prices will stay above this line and spend 40% of the time moving between this line and the 5/8 th's line.  
  
  
1/8 th Line (Weak, Stall and Reverse)  
This line is weak. If prices run down too far too fast, and if they stall at this line they will reverse up fast. If prices do not stall at this line they will move down to the 0/8 th's line. 

There is nothing in the Universe but mathematical points of force.

nice idea but Im afraid your calculations are wrong.

_Hint:  
From 105,41 to 106,73 is a degree of **11,53** 512° (not 45°)  
  
(SQRT(106,73) - SQRT(105,41)) x 180 = **11,53** 512°  
  
_

Personally I do not use the Gann grid tool - I use this [ICCE indicator](http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=5450158#post5450158) that I have been coding based on Bemac's work. The reason being that it is more flexible than the Gann grid. For example, I can decide to show only the rising diagonals and switch off the falling diagonals.   
  
Assuming Brooky comes back to the thread, I'll ask if he wants to use the same method instead of the Gann grid...failing that, I may write my own version....after improving the accuracy of the diagonals on the above mentioned indicator :nerd:

We are using __**astronomy**__ to measure time, because that is what we do on planet earth. Maybe you forgot about that. Remember, one day is one revolution of earth, takes 24 hours, 12 hours in a day, 12 in a night etc.  
  
Nobody here is using astrology.  
Astrology has to do with horoscopes and "feelings", astronomy with orbits and positions of planets.   
One is scientific the other is considered and art.   
  
Since there is nothing in the universe but science, we are using the scientific one but just to measure time, like mankind has done for many centuries now.  
  
Everything in the universe comes to an order, including the financial markets. That is what we are trying to profit from.

looking at D1 has its merits but looking for turns, M15, M5 may be needed. stop loss associated with bigger framer moves will be at levels different from those short term. the issue most people have is to identify when it turns or when it is going to hit the target. prices can overrun and overshoot esp. with the pump and dump activity. In any case, i believe there is no absolute certainty, it is question of raising confidence level and not looking for perfect system.  
  
i have used the fibo fann lines and before and at times, prices will hit and sometimes will serve to become resistance. in fact, i looked this for quite a while and noticed certain behvior and it is hard to explain.  
  
whether it is with gann, fibo, etc, it boils down to setting price and hitting the button when it matters, if we set a few targets, how would you place your sell price, it means we have to buy a few contracts or buy 1 contract and break the sell size at different levels.  
  
certain divergence pattern works, but you have to be there watching to catch it.  
  
What is the problem with big picture trading? I think will miss a lot of activites in between. When prices are sideways or ranging, and then it trends, the behaviors are different.

  * [#233](/thread/post/5592900#post5592900 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 20, 2012 6:01pm  Apr 20, 2012 6:01pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar191049_2.gif) godim](godim)

  * Joined Aug 2011 | Status: Trader | [4,005 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=191049)

From the above writings derive a few things.   
**First**. There are suppliers of quotations, which give details of the sixth bar a week. These graphics may NOT be used for our trading system. Data must be manipulated manually.   
**Second**. We can calculate the number of bars for each Time frame so that there is no break in time. For example, H4. Bars for a week = 5 days x 6 bars / day = 30 bars per week. For H1. Bars for a week = 5 days x 24 bars / day = 120 bars a week. Count bars for a week that you receive from your suppliers and determine which is the smallest Time frame without interruption in time. There will be continued.

  * [#240](/thread/post/5593419#post5593419 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 20, 2012 7:58pm  Apr 20, 2012 7:58pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar246273_8.gif) Vogon](vogon)

  * | Joined Apr 2012  | Status: Trader | [48 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=246273)

Would it negate the value of the Gann angle lines if we assume a constant flow of price time? This would certainly fix any differences in feeds etc.  
  
But this would create lines that shift with every break in trading on our charts.  
  
I'll defer to ILP on this point. we don't want to over complicate a working system.  
  
Concerning time frames, The choice of time frames would seem to have more of an impact on the divergent oscillator used for confirmation than the angle lines. The angle lines should be very consistent across all time frames. So perhaps we should use a higher time frame to confirm trend change and then switch to a lower time frame to trigger an entry off of an angle line. 

Thanks for all the fish

  * [#243](/thread/post/5593534#post5593534 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 20, 2012 8:27pm  Apr 20, 2012 8:27pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar191049_2.gif) godim](godim)

  * Joined Aug 2011 | Status: Trader | [4,005 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=191049)

Gann used three types of swings chart.  
  
"**One-Bar Swing Chart** (1-Bar Swing Chart): The One-Bar Swing Chart, or Minor Trend Chart, follows the one-bar movements of the market. From a low price, each time the market makes a higher-high than the previous bar, a One-Bar trend line moves up from the recent low to the new high. This action makes the previous low price a One-Bar bottom. From a high price each time the market makes a lower-low than the previous bar, a One-Bar swing line moves down from the recent high to the new low. This action makes the previous high price a One-Bar top.  
The combination of One-Bar tops and bottoms forms the One-Bar trend indicator chart. The crossing of a One-Bar swing top changes the One-Bar trend to up. The penetration of a One-Bar swing bottom changes the One-Bar trend to down."  
  
"**Two-Bar Swing Chart** (2-Bar Swing Chart): The Two-Bar Swing Chart, or Intermediate Trend Chart, follows the two-bar movements of the market. From a low price each time the market makes a higher-high than the previous bar for two consecutive time periods, a Two-Bar trend line moves up from the low two bars back to the new high. This action makes the low price from two bars back a Two-Bar Swing Bottom. From a high price each time the market makes a lower-low than the previous bar for two consecutive time periods, a Two-Bar trend line moves down from the high two bars back to the new low. This action makes the high price from two bars back a Two-Bar Swing Top.  
The combination of Two-Bar swing tops and bottoms forms the Two-Bar trend indicator chart. The crossing of a Two-Bar swing top changes the Two-Bar trend to up. The penetration of a Two-Bar trend bottom changes the Two-Bar trend to down."  
  
"**Main Trend** : The main trend swing chart follows the three-bar movements of the market from a low price each time the market makes a higher-high than the previous bar for three consecutive time periods, a main trend line moves up from the low three bars back to the new high. This action makes the low price from three bars back to a main bottom. From a high price each time the market makes a lower-low from the previous bar for three consecutive time periods, a main trend line moves down from the high three bars back to the new low. This action makes the high price from the three bars back a main top.  
The combination of main swing tops and bottoms forms the main trend indicator chart. The crossing of the main swing top changes the main swing to up. The penetration of a main swing bottom changes the main trend to down.  
Depending on trader preference, sometimes a two-bar swing is used to determine the main trend."  
  
Source: <http://patternpricetime.com/>

"You have to BE before you can DO, and DO before you can HAVE." Zig Ziglar

  * Apr 20, 2012 10:06pm  Apr 20, 2012 10:06pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar69410_4.gif) Ilovepippin](ilovepippin)

  * Joined May 2008 | Status: Gannalist | [1,176 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=69410)

I thought we wanted the 15m timeframe, but this works on all TFs.  
  
We ideally enter after a failed "new high or low".  
In EW terms this would be wave 2 or B.   
  
There are several indi's that give a signal.   
I have an indi that gives alternate buy/sell signals but this needs modification because ideally we reach an entry and lets say we are selling, then we keep selling on retraces as long as it keeps the trend.  
  
The difference with this method vs others is that when we enter against the "prevailing" trend in a wave 2 or B we can do so with a short stop and avoid the trap that other trendfollowing systems have since the majority of those systems would go with the trend on a "strong" buy/sell since all indi's that are trendfollowing are showing a strong trend.   
  
I would not use the swing indicator. It clogs up the screen.

turn off the Auto HiLo option in the indicator settings  
  
near the current candle on the chart should be a vertical red bar, when you double click the bar two endpoints and one midpoint should appear. drag the end points to the hi and low you like, then double click the chart to deselect the line. you can wait for MT4 to refresh or manually right click and refresh the chart to see the new grid.  
  
if you switch TFs you're gonna have to re do the red bar again, and manually delete the other TF red bar since it doesn't automatically disappear  
  
  
also like to add that one should play with the cycle #, it's set default at 34, but check out this chart with it set at 55, the second chart is a line version zoomed out so you can see past activity. magical numbers ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

I found the definition of vibration on Wikipedia.  
"Vibration is a mechanical phenomenon whereby oscillations occur about an equilibrium point. The oscillations may be periodic such as the motion of a pendulum or random such as the movement of a tire on a gravel road."  
<http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vibration>  
  
We must disregard the mechanical definition. Because the price is something imaginary. So I alter the definition.  
  
"Vibration is a phenomenon whereby oscillations the price occur about an equilibrium point. The oscillations may be periodic or random." 

"You have to BE before you can DO, and DO before you can HAVE." Zig Ziglar

  * [#257](/thread/post/5596171#post5596171 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 21, 2012 4:04pm  Apr 21, 2012 4:04pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar174081_3.gif) neuron](neuron)

  * | Joined Mar 2011  | Status: firing synapses catching pips | [856 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=174081)

_“From my extensive investigations, studies and applied  
tests, I find that not only do the various stocks vibrate, but  
that the driving forces controlling the stocks are also in a  
state of vibration”  
  
“Stocks, like atoms, are really centres of energies. Therefore,  
they are controlled mathematically…. There is no  
chance in nature because mathematical principles of the  
highest order lie at the foundation of all things”   
  
“The power to determine the trend of the market is due  
to my knowledge of the characteristics of each individual  
stock and a certain grouping of different stocks under their  
proper rates of vibration. Stocks are like electrons, atoms  
and molecules, which hold persistently to their own individuality  
in response to the fundamental Law Of Vibration….  
After exhaustive researches and investigations of  
the known sciences, I discovered that the Law Of Vibration  
enabled me to accurately determine the exact points  
to which stocks or commodities should rise and fall within  
a given time. The working out of this law determines the  
cause and predicts the effect long before the Street is aware  
of either”_  
  
  
  
these are all quotes of W.D. Gann.  
  
essentially, he believed that the behavior of commodity and stock prices could be mathematically determined based on research of past data that determined the unique vibration frequency  
  
this could be approached in a variety of manners, visually from drawing Gann fan trendlines to mathematical calculations of price from square of 9 (or in this case, an excel sheet with the appropriate formulas)  
  
the indicator for this PVS system provides mathematical calculations of potential price levels based on your input of hi and low data points, and a Gann grid is provided to plot potential turning points in the future (once properly calibrated)

"_I soon began to note the periodical recurrence of the rise and fall in stocks and commodities. This led me to conclude that natural law was the basis of market movements. I then decided to devote ten years of my life to the study of natural law as applicable to the speculative markets and to devote my best energies toward making speculation a profitable profession. After exhaustive researches and investigations of the known sciences, I discovered that the law of vibration enabled me to accurately determine the exact points at which stocks or commodities should rise and fall within a given time._ "  
  
  
"_The law which I have applied will not only give these long cycles or swings, but the daily and even hourly movements of stocks. By knowing the exact vibration of each individual stock I am able to determine at what point each will receive support and at what point the greatest resistance is to be met_."

  
  
"_Stocks are like electrons, atoms and molecules, which hold persistently to their own individuality in response to the fundamental law of vibration. [...] From my extensive investigations, studies and applied tests, I find that not only do the various stocks vibrate, but that the driving forces controlling the stocks are also in a state of vibration. These vibratory forces can only be known by the movements they generate on the stocks and their values in the market. Since all great swings or movements of the market are cyclic, they act in accordance with periodic law_."

  
  
"_If we wish to avert failure in speculation we must deal with causes. Everything in existence is based on exact proportion and perfect relationship. There is no chance in nature, because mathematical principles of the highest order lie at the foundation of all things. Faraday said, "**There is nothing in the universe but mathematical points of force**_."

  
  
  
"_Vibration is fundamental: nothing is exempt from this law. It is universal, therefore applicable to every class of phenomena on the globe._ " 

  
  
"_Through the law of vibration every stock in the market moves in its own distinctive sphere of activities, as to intensity, volume and direction; all the essential qualities of its evolution are characterized in its own rate of vibration. Stocks, like atoms, are really centres of energy; therefore, they are controlled mathematically. Stocks create their own field of action and power: power to attract and repel, which principle explains why certain stocks at times lead the market and 'turn dead' at other times. Thus, to speculate scientifically it is absolutely necessary to follow natural law_."

  
  
"**_After years of patient study I have proven to my entire satisfaction, as well as demonstrated to others, that vibration explains every possible phase and condition of the market._** "

  
  

W.D.Gann

  * Apr 21, 2012 5:30pm  Apr 21, 2012 5:30pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar191049_2.gif) godim](godim)

  * Joined Aug 2011 | Status: Trader | [4,005 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=191049)

I continue. In order to enable us to predict the vibrations of the price we must know the points of oscillation and the law under which oscillations are made. Right? Gann offers a way to determine these points - these are swing charts. And Gann offered through these points to build lines of fans from different angles. Finally Gann wrote a rule that describes the price oscillation between these lines.   
That is:  
"**Rule of All Angles** : Another important guideline is what Gann called the Rule of All Angles. When a market breaks an angle, it will move toward the next angle. This is because as time passes, an angle’s importance weakens and the market eventually breaks through. Therefore a market breaking the 2 x 1 angle will begin to move toward the 1 x 1 angle; just as a market breaking the 1 x 1 angle will eventually reach the 1 x 2 angle. Conversely, in an up move, an angle that holds the 1 x 2 angle is likely to rally to the 1 x 1, just as overtaking the 1 x 1 is likely to lead to a rally to the 2 x 1."  
Source:  
[http://patternpricetime.com/glossary...of-all-angles/](http://patternpricetime.com/glossary/r/rule-of-all-angles/)  
  
How does the chart aud/usd:

If we read them carefully we will find important keys. For example Gann said that:  
a)Each financial instrument has its own vibration.  
b) Knowing specific vibration of a financial instrument help us determine in which point they will find support or resistance.  
c)Knowing the vibration allows us to understand the structure of the market,in which phase it is found and in which phase the market is in.  
I underline,not in the strict meaning of the definition but in the definition of the concept of vibration.  
Obviously this is only my point of view,and each can approach things in his own way.

  * [#270](/thread/post/5596332#post5596332 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 21, 2012 7:49pm  Apr 21, 2012 7:49pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar113418_3.gif) matei](matei)

  * | Commercial User  | Joined Aug 2009 | [824 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=113418)

Nirestein said:-To measure its frequency of oscillation or vibratory rate which never changes (going from High to Low). The result is just to get a matematical number from any chart.  
To get a chart Pitched(slope) True- so that a 45 degree angle is really 45 degree.  
Go to historical chart, take the highest price point, subtract price of Snap- Back to Declining Tops line.  
Take the number of Trading Days from High point to Snap-Back point.  
Getting arihmetic of 1 x 2 line= (p1-p2)/trading days  
ex![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f641.png?v=15.1)400-300)/200=100/200=.5 units per day.  
So the 1x2 angle has a value of .5 units per day- Doubling it will give you the 1x1, which is 1 price unit per day.  
This is the way you scale price units on chart.  
"rising above the 1x2 angle puts commodities in a strong position where strong rallies should ensue"-W.D.Gann  
Once you have a True Pitched chart-find price Symmetry above and below the **Nodal Line**.Using a compass, swing High and Low symmetrically around the X axis (price). This will NOT work on a Non-Piched True chart.  
Breaking one angle takes you down to the next angle-this is where you expect to find support.Does Not mean there will be a Change of Trend, but just Support.  
1x2 angle: once you break it, you will return to the Base therefore, the 1x2 angle is called the "Death Angle"

  * [ Oshawa](oshawa)

  * | Joined Jul 2009  | Status: Trader | [454 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=107751)

I genuinely hope people can pay a little bit attention to their reading. Regarding Gann angles or Gann Fan, it's all been very clearly explained in materials in a few simple sentences of a very clear example, within a book of about 99 pages including all the padding and appendix. The attached chart shows two sets of Gann angle lines: red and yellow. The red ones are drawn based on some of the discussion here that one has to take two low points A&B(one original one snap back) and calculate the time inbetween. The yellow ones are calculated from one single point only, ie point A. You can see they're nearly identical. But which one can be identified much earlier, it's up to you to judge.  
  
Allonso, I don't think you should be disappointed. What they're saying is all very helpful if you have no previous knowledge on the Gann subject. And what's all the fuss about finding a turning point in time? What about a turning point in price? Do you think it's easier to set an order on your platform with a price to go long or short or easier to phone your broker and tell them to enter on your behalf once the clock hits 1430? I am not aware of any platform that can allow one to preset entry order by time only. Gann might seem all mysterious touting about time, and it plays with our psyche that the more mysterious it is the better or more fascinating it must be. Price is time, and time is also price, if one likes to quote Gann. Forget about all the philosophical issues about time, for trading purpose only, I will take price anyday and anytime.

  * [#278](/thread/post/5596445#post5596445 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 21, 2012 10:16pm  Apr 21, 2012 10:16pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar191049_2.gif) godim](godim)

  * Joined Aug 2011 | Status: Trader | [4,005 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=191049)

But this is not the problem with MT4. There are very different angles. This can be understood only if you work very precisely and have calculations with a calculator. For now, take it on trust. Later you will be able to see for yourself.   
1\. [90 - (45/8)] = 84.375  
2\. [90 - (45/4)] = 78.750  
3\. [90 - (45/3)] = 75.000  
4\. [90 - (45/2)] = 67.500  
5\. 45 = 45.000  
6\. 45/2 = 22.500  
7\. 45/3 = 15.000  
8\. 45/4 = 11.250  
9\. 45/8 = 5.625 

"You have to BE before you can DO, and DO before you can HAVE." Zig Ziglar

  * Apr 21, 2012 10:49pm  Apr 21, 2012 10:49pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar191049_2.gif) godim](godim)

  * Joined Aug 2011 | Status: Trader | [4,005 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=191049)

If we calculate tan() of these angles will receive and their coefficients. They differ from those used by Gann. Now occur the following problem. If you want to work with right angles of Gann, we must render the whole fan angle after angle. That means nine angles with different coefficients. And each of them can be curved in its own direction. I prefer to work with the fan of MT4, and add two lines of Gann for 2x1 and 1x2. The angles are 11.

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar69410_4.gif) Ilovepippin](ilovepippin)

  * Joined May 2008 | Status: Gannalist | [1,176 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=69410)

> [Quoting Oshawa](/thread/post/5596438#post5596438 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I genuinely hope people can pay a little bit attention to their reading. Regarding Gann angles or Gann Fan, it's all been very clearly explained in materials in a few simple sentences of a very clear example, within a book of about 99 pages including all the padding and appendix. The attached chart shows two sets of Gann angle lines: red and yellow. The red ones are drawn based on some of the discussion here that one has to take two low points A&B(one original one snap back) and calculate the time inbetween. The yellow ones are calculated from one...
> 
> Ignored

Thank you Oshawa, this is the correct method and as I said before for Forex that translates to 1 day for 1 cent or 100 pips on a 4 digit platform. for the 1x1 or 45 degree angle (aspect).  
  
This needs to be added to the Moneydeep Indi.  
  
BTW. The moneydeep indicator does not let you move the line with the (HiLo) function on false. Maybe that can be fixed. Thanks.  
  
Matei: Gann used code language. Angle = Aspect, price = time  
So if you know the "angle" of a stock you will know where (at which price) it will turn (when time and price meet, and they meet at an angle)  
However, here we are trying to follow the trend until it turns.   
Buy when it goes up, sell when it goes down.   
  
In the end you get the same result as Gann. Gann knew when price was going to turn, but then he had to confirm the turn. That means he did not get into the market at the point that price and time met, but when he confirmed that it reacted according to his forecast.   
Well, you can do the same thing without the complicated forecast and get a high probability trade as I described earlier.

This is not correct. As I also thought this when I first tried it.  
The control bar is very close to the last bar of the chart and is often difficult to see. There is another bar (not sure of its function) that you can not move.  
  
Also I have found that if you place the control bar from a High to a Low and take that price length and calculate the proper time length for a square and place that value into the Cycle_Bars parameter. You will get a near perfect 1x1 line. Any deviation is caused by fractional values.

How to calculate MurrayMath levels? You we will use the indicator?   
But how to calculate time in fractals is important. This will calculate the time. And then we will submit it to the indicator.   
Finally. If you fill in the table can get the probability of reversal for each leg.

Hi All.  
  
Originally I coded the first indicators to help MoneyDeep out and the thread has evolved into quite a discussion in many areas, probably because of it's misnomer as a price vibration system which tends to conjure up other ideas aside from Gann. Not a spot for newbies who are wanting the holy grail arrow but certainly a melting pot of ideas with much good information so a big thanks to all who have taken the time to post their ideas etc.  
  
As promised I am posting an indicator that has evolved from the original MoneyDeep levels. I am aware that there are divisions of thought about what is right and wrong re Gann levels angles etc and am sure that the indicator is both right and wrong depending on your point of view.  
  
I post it here to keep my word but as many are aware I do not trade specifically with this indicator and it is posted as a possible aid to those who use it. I do know of one high end trader who does use it effectively and sings it's praises. Thanks to those that have pm'd me and contributed to it's development.  
  
I simply do not have the time to support this indicator so please do not pm me or ask for changes as I am knee deep in other work, but the code is open and anyone with a bit of coding experience will be able to change anything as needed.  
  
I have also included an update to the range finder indicator. The color was not able to be reset and can be now.  
  
Inside the zip file is an instruction pdf on how to use the indicator. Please READ it before loading it. The instructions were written as I was doing V3, but apply to V4.  
  
You will need a ticker on weekends to make any sense of it. It's a monster of a thing, but once loaded it appears to settle down nicely. It is not the sort of indi you drag around the charts every minute. take the time to set it up and then work with it as a background map for a few days at a time.  
  
So with that said, success to all.  
Cheers  
Brooky.

  * Joined Aug 2011 | Status: Trader | [4,005 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=191049)

We must add the time scale. I use MT4 modified instrument. Fibo TimeZones. Simply fill levels 0,1,2,3,4,5,6,7 and 8. And descriptions 0,1,2,3,4,5,6,7 and 8. Then make the first division equal to 32 days.

  * [#304](/thread/post/5597457#post5597457 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 22, 2012 5:01pm  Apr 22, 2012 5:01pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar191049_2.gif) godim](godim)

  * Joined Aug 2011 | Status: Trader | [4,005 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=191049)

What to do? We need to change the scale of the chart.   
To do this let us calculate the the scale of the price over time. How? Simply. take one unit of price and divide it one unit of time. A division of time is 32 days. We need to work with bars. For those of you who will try to M15. One division on the price is 10010 - 9766 = 244 pips. So the scale (vibration) is 244/32 = 7.625 pips/day  
How to use this? Let's build Gann Grid. 

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: audusd.gif
Size: 84 KB](/attachment/image/947088/thumbnail?d=1365759674)](/attachment/image/947088?d=1335081665)   

"You have to BE before you can DO, and DO before you can HAVE." Zig Ziglar

Suppose 10 cents per 1/8 inch. Putting the entire table or table part of the diagram. This is the graph until the beginning. Then every day inflict new data taken from the exchange. And let's assume that after one or two years the price out of range.   
What to do now?

  * Apr 28, 2012 7:04pm  Apr 28, 2012 7:04pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar191049_2.gif) godim](godim)

  * Joined Aug 2011 | Status: Trader | [4,005 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=191049)

I use the divisions of MurreyMath to determine the price scale. I ask one-year interval of the cycle and MutteyMath determine the range in price. This occur difficulty for the Study of the price range for one-year interval of past times. Because the indicator is designed to calculate from the current time ago. In other words I can not determine price range for the one-year interval for the date 31/12/2011. But this difficulty can be overcome by using the Strategy Tester. Set a daily graphics and the last date 31/12/2011. On the resulting graph place indicator MurreyMath for one year. So you can explore the one-year price range back to this one, until you price information. Finally, we must decide what the scale of the price over time (vibration).

  * Apr 28, 2012 7:27pm  Apr 28, 2012 7:27pm

In eur/usd I calculated level of 15.25 pips/day. Accept it for the all cases of change of the price range. Like Gann's charts was plotted on paper. Then the calculations are different. Let's take the current situation. The price range has shrunk so that one division was 244 pips. Because I want to keep the scale of 15.25 pips/day. Calculate a new length of the cycle. [244/15,25] x 8 = 16 x 8 = 128 days.

  * [#347](/thread/post/5633128#post5633128 "Post Permalink")

  * May 3, 2012 6:12pm  May 3, 2012 6:12pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar124529_2.gif) brooky29](brooky29)

  * | Commercial User  | Joined Nov 2009 | [51 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=124529)

Hi All,  
  
I owe a debt of gratitude to one particular trader who has pursued me to understand the V4 indicator. Without his dogged persistence the following problem would never have been found. Interesting to see that Neuron's chart above exhibits the problem perfectly but it is a little talked about or known anomaly in MT4.  
  
The issue lies with the different way that MT4 scales Arcs and Ellipses between 4 and 5 digit brokers. We are all aware of the point difference this cause re price, but certainly to myself ... and I can guarantee to many other coders not the scaling issue.  
  
The effect is that as per Neurons chart above, if you are using a 5 digit broker, the arcs and ellipses are all squashed horizontally and extended far to the left and right. The same chart that Neuron has would appear totally different with the circles being round and squared correctly to the box. This of course makes a huge difference re Gann trading.  
  
The solution has been found and I have added an automatic feature in this update so that irrespective of your broker, the arcs will/should display correctly.  
  
I suggest the lights will suddenly go on for many traders who are using the indi on 5 digit brokers.  
  
Another point that came out of my discussions with this trader was that people need to pay attention to the comments to achieve correct squareness. I have added the tpl of the chart below to help someone understand what settings are needed to achieve the result on chart. Other settings of course are square as well such as an 84 pip box height, 42 size cycle and Auto cycle of 2. It's just a question of ratios.  
  
Place the tpl on AUDUSD H1 and have a look at the settings as a matter of interest.  
  
The picture is on [Oanda](/brokers/oanda "View OANDA Broker Profile") 5 Digit broker.  
  
Cheers  
Brooky

  * [#353](/thread/post/5640088#post5640088 "Post Permalink")

  * May 5, 2012 10:52pm  May 5, 2012 10:52pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar124529_2.gif) brooky29](brooky29)

  * | Commercial User  | Joined Nov 2009 | [51 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=124529)

Hi All,  
  
It has come to my attention from aforementioned diligent trader who watches over me that the MoneyDeepLevelsAutoShadedV4.1.mq4 ( last version) indeed works much better re scaling, but has an issue with larger time frames. H4. Daily etc in displaying relevant timely arcs.  
  
The reason for this is that the indi was originally designed with the 1 pip 1 bar squaring idea and other logic layered over that.  
  
The above is not an issue in timeframes up to H1 where there are plenty of bars and most pullbacks measured are somewhere around the 100 - 200 pip range. The square simply expands to that amount of bars.  
  
In Daily though, ranges over 1000 + are often measured and that means that one firstly needs a large amount of bars in Daily history, and the arcs can span many weeks ahead. Too much so in fact to feel confident about using these Daily levels or Arcs in analysis.  
  
Therefore the indicator has been enhanced to offer scaling in the pips to bar area. This in essence means that you can square off a 1000 pip range over for eg a 100 bar time range and generate much tighter but perfectly squared Arcs that are much more relevant as opposed to the 1 to 1 scaling previously where you needed 1000 bars to square.  
  
The actual amplitude of the arcs has been brought out of code as an option that should not need to be changed but gives one the ability too should one wish to.  
  
You will see additions in the options as below. For larger tf's, just change the PipBarRatio option and everything else will/should :-) adjust. Comments have been enhanced to include this information.  
  
extern string PipBarNote1 = "One means square to 1bar per pip";  
extern string PipBarNote2 = "4 means square to 1 bar per 4 pips";  
extern string PipBarNote3 = "Set 10 for Daily TF Recommended";  
**extern int PipBarRatio = 1;** // Set to 10 as eg for daily.  
  
  
Arc scaling that should NOT need to be changed.  
extern string ScaleNote1 = "4 digit Brokers..EllipseScale = 1";  
extern string ScaleNote2 = "4 digit Brokers..ArcScale = 1";  
extern string ScaleNote3 = "5 digit Brokers..EllipseScale = 0.1";  
extern string ScaleNote4 = "5 digit Brokers..ArcScale = 10";  
extern string ScaleNote5 = "Can Custom Scale To Suit";  
  
extern double SetEllipseScale = 0.1;  
extern double SetArcScale = 10;  
  
The indicator and a tpl on AUDUSD Daily are attached below so you can see how the settings can work.  
  
The 1st example picture below shows what can be achieved in Daily now that was impossible before.  
  
The 2nd example is of how the settings now could work in a projected Daily mode where we make the square incomplete ( therefore the Gray square hides to the left ) while the arcs and epicentre are projected forward.  
  
You will also notice in the second picture that the cycles per square are set at 3 instead of the traditional 2 or 4.   
  
I encourage traders to have two charts set the same tf's etc, but one with either the 2nd or 4th harmonic and the other with the 3rd or 5th harmonic.   
  
It is a known natural occurance that these harmonic cycles will alternate as time progresses. You will find yourself with many more trading opportunities if you pay attention to which harmonic price is respecting at that point in time.   
  
If you really want, you can add the minor 7th harmonic and you will have the majority of twists and turns, pullback's etc nailed that the market can offer. Confluence of these harmonics is as powerful as Fibonacci confluence, but in reality they are all tapping into the same Vibe.  
  
Many possibilities are now available within the indicator and hopefully this last release should cater for most needs.  
  
Cheers  
Brooky

> [Quoting angelofx](/thread/post/5646101#post5646101 "View Quoted Post")
