> 
> Brooky is the AUDUSD template applicable to other currency pairs or is it limited to only AUDUSD...
> 
> Ignored

Hi  
  
The template was designed to show how to achieve certain scaling and I only used AUDUSD because it was open.  
  
If you want to use the same settings on eg: H1 EURUSD, all you have to do is open your EURUSD chart and apply the AUDUSD template.  
  
**At that point it will make no sense at all** because the control bar is set to AUDUSD prices.  
  
Right click the chart and select Objects. Find the ControlBar object and select edit.  
Just enter in some prices you can see on your chart to get the control bar on screen somewhere in front of you.  
  
Then drag it to some relevant points and all the scaling etc of the AUDUSD template is intact.  
Then save the template as EURUSD_H1 or so and you will not have to do it again.  
  
Pics below of the change and the new EURUSD chart using the AUDUSD template.  
  
  
Cheers  
Brooky

#  [](/thread/308230-gann-pvs-price-vibration-system-trading)Gann PVS (Price vibration System) Trading

  * Jun 5, 2012 5:41pm  Jun 5, 2012 5:41pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar111000_7.gif) One day!](member.php?u=111000)

Well I plumped for pips per bar in the end.....  
  

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: 4X_GANN_FAN.png
Size: 50 KB](/attachment/image/976620/thumbnail?d=1365767883)](/attachment/image/976620?d=1338884861)   

  
  
I think that the use of the indicator is fairly straightforward, but I have put a short [video](http://www.screencast.com/t/e9JfcGW6fBJ) together to demonstrate setting up etc,.  
  
The one grey area is deciding on how many pips per daily bar to use, that I'll leave to the individual...referring to the video you will see that I used 10pips on the EURUSD chart, however, some of the lower timeframes will need different values - 10pip per day on a 1min chart is too flat in my opinion. On the subject of different timeframes, I would recommend setting up the fans on the timeframe that you want to use them - it is possible to drop down and go up, but this exposes the issue with bar open times - a bar open time on one timeframe may not be present on another timeframe.  
  
Anyway, try it out if you like and let me know if you find any bugs.... 

Attached File(s)

>  The template was designed to show how to achieve certain scaling and I only used AUDUSD because it was open.  
>    
>  If you want to use the same settings on eg: H1 EURUSD, all you have to do is open your EURUSD chart and apply the AUDUSD template.  
>    
>  **At that point it will make no sense at all** because the control bar is set to AUDUSD prices.  
>    
>  Right click the chart and select Objects. Find the ControlBar object and select edit.  
>  Just enter in some prices you can see on your chart to get the control bar on screen somewhere in front of you.  
>    
>  Then...

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar111000_7.gif) One day!](member.php?u=111000)

  * | Joined Jul 2009  | Status: ...or there about! | [220 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=111000)

> [Quoting makefortune](/thread/post/5729186#post5729186 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> After the rays are setup, I try to move them, but i end up dragging one line instead of the bunch of the lines at the location. Did I miss something in your demo?
> 
> Ignored

It sounds as though you may have selected one of the trendlines instead of the price marker. They are quite fiddly to select but if you hover your mouse over the right of the marker you should see a little info box with the name of the object - the markers and trendlines have different names. When you have selected the marker, you just move that to the required location.   
  
The speed at which the fan redraws is entirely dependent on incoming ticks, so if the market is slow, just use the standard chart refresh.  
  
Hope the above clarifies?...

The authors plotted the fan using the lines through two points. One is the point of beginning. The other is calculated for the current date and the corresponding coefficients of 1x1, 1x2, etc. So the graph is correct. But I am accustomed to look just like that. And the fans are symmetrical.

I have tried to explain it. It depends on a division of MurreyMath a daily chart for one year. Now this division is 244 pips. Two years ago was 488 pips. These 488 pips to divide them 1/8 year - or 32 days. And get pips 15.25 per day.
